The meaning of 'ala for obligation in Hanafi Usul
Defines 'ala as indicating obligation with example from aman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the Arabic preposition 'ala indicates a binding obligation in debt-related statements and apply this principle to derive rulings in contracts and aman grants.

Core Idea
'ala on debt means obligation; 'indee does not.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the precise meaning of prepositions carries significant legal weight. The word 'ala does not always indicate obligation; its meaning depends on context. This lesson examines when 'ala signals a binding duty, using an example from al-Siyar al-Kabir about granting aman to a group. By mastering this distinction, you will understand how a single word can shift legal rights and obligations.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the term 'ala in context
Identify the Arabic preposition 'ala in a statement involving a debt or financial obligation. Note that it is often used in phrases like 'alayhi dayn (he has a debt on him).
The word appears in structures indicating what one owes.
2
Distinguish 'ala from other prepositions
Contrast 'ala with words like 'indee (with me), ma'ee (with me), and qabli (in my possession). The passage states that these do not indicate obligation; only 'ala does in debt contexts.
Memorize the four prepositions: 'ala (obligation), 'indee/ma'ee/qabli (possession).
3
Understand the effect of elevation (ta'allī)
The word 'ala literally means elevation or superiority. In legal terms, this implies authority and responsibility, which translates into a binding duty when used for debt.
The root meaning helps derive the legal effect.
4
Apply to the aman example
Apply the meaning of 'ala to the head of fortress requesting aman for ten people. Because he used 'ala, he retains the right to designate which ten. If he had used 'and' or 'then', the granter designates.
Work through the example step by step.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في على
أي إفادته التعلى
ألف" يحمَلُ على الدين، بخلاف ما لو قال: "عندي أو معي أو قبلي". وعلى هذا قال في "السير" الكبير" : إذا قال رأس الحصن " آمَنُوني على عشرة من أهل الحصن" ففعلنا، فالعشرة سواه، وخيار التعيين له، ولو قال: "آمنوني وعشرة أو فعشرةً، أو ثُمَّ عشرة" ففعَلْنا فكذلك، وخيار التعيين للآمن.
Chapter on 'ala: meaning of elevation. 'Alf' is interpreted as debt, contrary to if he said: 'indee or ma'ee or qabli.' And based on this, it is said in al-Siyar al-Kabir: If the head of the fortress said: 'Grant me aman on ten people of the fortress' and we did so, the ten are others besides him, and the choice of designation is for him. And if he said: 'Grant me aman and ten, or then ten' and we did so, similarly, and the choice of designation is for the one who grants aman.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a legal definition and ruling. It explains that the word 'ala when used in the context of financial obligations (like debt) indicates a duty, unlike words like 'indee which imply custody. The example from al-Siyar al-Kabir illustrates: when the head of a fortress requests aman 'on ten people' using 'ala, he has the right to designate which ten, because 'ala gives him superiority. If he uses 'and' or 'then', the aman-giver designates. This is a Hanafi ruling based on the literal meaning of 'ala for elevation and obligation.

Key Terms
على ('ala): preposition that can indicate obligation when used with debt
التعلى (al-ta'allī): elevation or superiority implied by the word 'ala

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the aman example, what is the ruling if the head of the fortress uses 'ala when requesting aman for ten people?
A) The aman-giver designates the ten
B) The head designates the ten
C) The ten are chosen by lot
D) No aman is granted

Key Takeaway
The preposition 'ala in debt contexts indicates a binding obligation, and its use can shift legal authority, as shown in the aman ruling.

The Meaning of 'Ala as Condition: The Talaq Dispute
Analyses 'ala as condition with talaq dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that 'ala indicates condition (shart) when there is sequence, and evaluate the Sahibayn's counterargument based on exchange (mu'awada).

Core Idea
'Ala indicates condition when result follows cause; without simultaneity, there is no exchange.

This lesson analyzes a classic ikhtilaf in Hanafi usul: whether the word 'ala in a conditional divorce operates as a condition (shart) or as an exchange (mu'awada). The ruling has practical consequences: if a wife says 'divorce me three times for a thousand,' and the husband divorces only once, does she owe anything? We will trace the linguistic and usul reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term and its possible meanings
The word 'ala can mean 'upon' (condition) or 'in exchange for'. In the verse (60:12), it means 'on condition that'. In the talaq case, it is ambiguous.
Hanafi usul: when a term has multiple meanings, the default is the literal meaning unless context indicates otherwise.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his usul reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that 'ala here indicates condition because divorce and payment are sequential: divorce occurs first, then payment is due. This sequence matches the pattern of condition and result (shart wa jaza).
Sequence: divorce (first) -> money (second). This is not simultaneous, so not exchange.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their linguistic interpretation
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad interpret 'ala as 'bi' (in exchange), making it a mu'awada. They argue that divorce for money is an exchange from the woman's side, so each talaq deserves one-third of the sum.
They rely on qiyas to a sale contract where price is for each unit.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds that exchange requires simultaneity (muqabala bi la tartib). Since divorce and payment are not simultaneous, 'ala cannot mean exchange; it must mean condition.
The key distinction: mu'awada demands mutual obligation at the same moment.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical difference: if husband divorces once, Abu Hanifa says no money; Sahibayn say one-third. The text (wa lahu) indicates Abu Hanifa's view is preferred (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يكون "على" بمعنى الشرط، قال الله تعالى: يُبَا عَنكَ عَلَى أَنْ لَا يُشْرِكْنَ بِاللَّهِ شَيْئًا ،
ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة يليه : إذا قالت لزوجها: "طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف" فطلقها واحدةً لا يجب المال؛ لأن الكلمة ههنا تفيد معنى الشرط، فيكون الثلاث شرطاً للزوم المال.
لا يجب المال: وهو ألف للزوج، وقال أبو يوسف و محمد رحمها يجب ثلث الألف. فيكون الثلاث إلخ: فإنه إذا طلقها الرجل واحدة لا يجب شيء من المال؛ لأن الشرط إذا فات وهو الثلاث فات المشروط أي المال، وعندهما: يجب ثلث الألف كما لو قالت: طلقني ثلاثاً بالألف؛ لأن الطلاق على المال معاوضة من جانب المرأة، والمال يجب عليها عوضاً عن الطلاق، فيحمل كلمة "على" بمعنى "الباء"، وقال أبو حنيفة له: ليس بين الطلاق وبين المال مقابلة لينعقد معاوضة بل بينهما معاقبة؛ لأن الطلاق يجب أولاً ثم يجب المال؛ لأن المال يجب أولاً ثم يقع الطلاق، وهذا معنى الشرط والجزاء لا معنى المعاوضة؛ لأن العوض يجب مقابلاً للمعوض معاً بلا ترتيب تحقيقاً للمقابلة، ويحمل على الشرط، فيكون الثلاث شرطاً للزوم المال، فإذا طلقها واحدة لم يوجد الشرط، فلم يلزم المال كذا في "المعدن".
And 'ala may be in the meaning of condition, Allah said: '... taking covenant from you that they shall not associate anything with Allah'. For this reason Abu Hanifa said: If a woman said to her husband: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand' and he divorced her once, the money is not obligatory because the word here indicates the meaning of condition, so three is a condition for the obligation of money. The money is not obligatory: it is a thousand for the husband. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: one-third of a thousand is obligatory. So three etc.: when the husband divorced her once, nothing of the money is obligatory because when the condition (three) is missing, the conditioned (money) is missing. According to them, one-third of a thousand is obligatory as if she said: 'Divorce me three times with a thousand', because divorce for money is an exchange from the woman's side, and the money is obligatory on her in exchange for divorce, so the word 'ala is interpreted in the meaning of 'bi'. And Abu Hanifa said: There is no mutual correspondence between divorce and money to constitute an exchange, but rather between them is sequence, because divorce is first then money is obligatory? Actually the money is first then divorce occurs, and this is the meaning of condition and result, not exchange, because compensation must be in return for the compensated simultaneously without order to realize exchange. So it is interpreted as condition, so three is condition for obligation of money. When he divorced her once, the condition is not found, so money is not obligatory. As in al-Ma'din.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a legal dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning the interpretation of the word 'ala in a conditional divorce. Abu Hanifa holds that 'ala here indicates a condition (shart): the wife's payment of one thousand is conditional on the husband giving three talags. If he only gives one, no money is due. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that 'ala should be interpreted as 'bi' (in exchange), making it a mu'awada (exchange contract), so each talaq deserves one-third of the thousand. Abu Hanifa's proof: divorce and money are not simultaneous; the money is conditioned on the occurrence of divorce, which is sequential, so 'ala indicates condition. The Hanafi position is that the word 'ala in such contexts is interpreted on its literal meaning (istihsan?) and that the contract is not an exchange because there is no simultaneity. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
على ('ala): can indicate condition (shart) resulting in a sequential relation
معاوضة (mu'awaḍah): exchange where both parties give and receive simultaneously

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One-thousand
C) One-third
D) Half

Key Takeaway
The word 'ala yields shart (condition) when the actions are sequential; when simultaneous, it can mean exchange (mu'awada).

Interpreting 'على' in Divorce for Payment: Condition or Exchange?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interpreting 'على' in divorce for payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of interpreting the word 'على' in a divorce-for-payment context as indicating condition, and derive the ruling when fewer than three divorces occur, contrasting with the Sahibayn's exchange interpretation.

Core Idea
The word 'على' in divorce for payment indicates condition, not exchange, due to the sequential nature of the acts.

This lesson dissects a classic usul dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) over a single word: 'على' in a wife's statement 'Divorce me three times for one thousand.' At stake is whether the payment is due if the husband divorces only once. Abu Hanifa sees a condition (the three divorces are a prerequisite for payment), while the Sahibayn see an exchange (each divorce triggers a proportional payment). The dispute hinges on whether the word 'على' is interpreted literally as indicating condition or metaphorically as indicating exchange (like 'ب'), and on the broader usul principle of carrying words to their literal meaning unless context overrides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed wording and its context
The wife says 'طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف' (Divorce me three times for one thousand). The key word is 'على', which in Arabic can indicate a condition (e.g., 'if you do X, then Y') or an exchange (e.g., 'I give you X in return for Y'). Identify the two possible interpretations.
Focus on the preposition and its legal implications.
2
State the two positions and their rulings
Abu Hanifa: 'على' indicates condition, so the payment (thousand) is due only if all three divorces occur. If the husband divorces once, nothing is due. Sahibayn: 'على' indicates exchange, so the payment is proportionally due: one-third of the thousand for one divorce.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is clear: husband's liability differs.
3
Analyze the linguistic and logical basis of each position
Abu Hanifa argues that the relationship between divorce and payment is sequential (معاقبة), not simultaneous. Exchange (معاوضة) requires simultaneity of consideration and countervalue. Since the divorce happens first (or payment first, but with a sequence), it is a condition, not an exchange. The Sahibayn argue that 'على' in this context is equivalent to 'ب' (with), signalling an exchange contract.
This step applies the usul principle of carrying words to their literal meaning (haqiqah) unless a contextual clue (qarinah) directs otherwise.
4
Derive the usul principle at play
The dispute reflects a deeper usul principle: How to interpret a word that has both a literal (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz) meaning? Abu Hanifa prefers the literal meaning (condition) because no overriding context forces the metaphorical exchange meaning. The Sahibayn see the context of 'divorce for payment' as a qarinah that shifts meaning to exchange.
This is related to the principle of 'al-asl fi al-kalam al-haqiqah' (the default in speech is the literal meaning).
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence: one divorce yields no payment (Abu Hanifa) vs. one-third (Sahibayn). The text presents Abu Hanifa's view as relied upon ('ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة'), indicating tarjih. Understand why Abu Hanifa's reasoning is considered stronger in the Hanafi school.
The tarjih is based on preserving the literal meaning and the sequential nature of the acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : إذا قالت لزوجها: "طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف" فطلقها واحدةً لا يجب المال؛ لأن الكلمة ههنا تفيد معنى الشرط، فيكون الثلاث شرطاً للزوم المال. لا يجب المال: وهو ألف للزوج، وقال أبو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله يجب ثلث الألف. فيكون الثلاث إلخ: فإنه إذا طلقها الرجل واحدة لا يجب شيء من المال؛ لأن الشرط إذا فات وهو الثلاث فات المشروط أي المال، وعندهما: يجب ثلث الألف كما لو قالت: طلقني ثلاثاً بالألف؛ لأن الطلاق على المال معاوضة من جانب المرأة، والمال يجب عليها عوضاً عن الطلاق، فيحمل كلمة "على" بمعنى "الباء"، وقال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله: ليس بين الطلاق وبين المال مقابلة لينعقد معاوضة بل بينهما معاقبة؛ لأن الطلاق يجب أولاً ثم يجب المال؛ لأن المال يجب أولاً ثم يقع الطلاق، وهذا معنى الشرط والجزاء لا معنى المعاوضة؛ لأن العوض يجب مقابلاً للمعوض معاً بلا ترتيب تحقيقاً للمقابلة، ويحمل على الشرط، فيكون الثلاث شرطاً للزوم المال، فإذا طلقها واحدة لم يوجد الشرط، فلم يلزم المال كذا في "المعدن".
And for this reason Abu Hanifa said: If a woman says to her husband, 'Divorce me three times for one thousand,' and he divorces her once, the payment is not obligatory because the word here conveys the meaning of condition, so the three (divorces) are a condition for the necessity of the payment. The payment is not obligatory: meaning the thousand for the husband. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: one-third of the thousand is obligatory. 'So the three etc.': because if the man divorces her once, none of the money is due; because when the condition (three divorces) is lost, the conditional thing (payment) is lost. According to them (the two), one-third of the thousand is due, just as if she said, 'Divorce me three times for one thousand,' because divorce for payment is a exchange from the woman's side, and the payment is due on her in exchange for the divorce, so the word 'على' is interpreted in the sense of 'الباء' (with). Abu Hanifa said: There is no correspondence between divorce and payment to constitute an exchange; rather there is a sequence between them, because divorce is first obligatory, then payment (in his view) or payment is first then divorce occurs (in their view). This is the meaning of condition and result, not exchange, because the consideration must be given in exchange for the countervalue simultaneously without sequence to achieve correspondence. So it is interpreted as condition, and three divorces are a condition for the necessity of the payment. So if he divorces her once, the condition is not fulfilled, so the payment is not obligatory, as in al-Ma'dan.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the interpretation of the word 'على' in a wife's statement: 'Divorce me three times for one thousand.' The key issue is whether the word 'على' indicates an exchange (معاوضة) or a condition (شرط). According to Abu Hanifa, it indicates a condition, so the payment is only due if all three divorces occur. The Sahibayn hold that it indicates an exchange, so the payment is divided proportionally. The reasoning: Abu Hanifa sees a sequence (معاقبة) between the actions (divorce and payment), not simultaneity required for exchange. Thus, the three divorces are a condition for the payment. The Sahibayn argue that 'على' is like 'ب' in an exchange contract, so payment is due for each divorce.

Key Terms
معاوضة (muʿāwaḍah): A mutual exchange contract where consideration and countervalue are simultaneous.
معاقبة (muʿāqabah): A sequence where one action occurs after the other, not simultaneously.

D) The divorce is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The word 'على' in divorce for payment is interpreted as condition (شرط) in the Hanafi school, based on the sequential nature of the acts, leading to the ruling that payment is only due when the full number of divorces is executed.

Interpreting 'في' in Temporal Divorce Conditions: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Dispute on the implication of 'في' in temporal divorce pronouncements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule regarding the particle 'في' in temporal contexts to determine the scope of a divorce pronouncement and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument.

Core Idea
Without 'في', the time word encompasses the whole; with 'في', a part suffices - ambiguity is accepted.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi examines a key dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the interpretation of the particle 'في' (in) when used with time words in divorce. The practical consequence affects whether a husband's intention to specify a part of the day is accepted in court. This linguistic-legal analysis sharpens your ability to identify how subtle textual features ('في' vs. direct connection) alter the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verbal act and the disputed particle
The act is a divorce pronouncement: 'You are divorced tomorrow' vs. 'You are divorced in tomorrow'. The particle 'في' is either omitted or mentioned.
2
State the position of the Sahibayn
They consider both phrases equivalent: both imply the entire day. An intention to specify a part is not accepted in court but only in conscience.
This is the opposing view within the Hanafi school.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and his key distinction
He distinguishes: without 'في', the verb directly attaches to the adverbial, resembling a direct object, thus requiring encompassment (full day). With 'في', it is a container, and encompassment is not required, so the time is ambiguous.
4
Apply the analogy to fasting
The same principle applies to 'I will fast the entire time' vs. 'I will fast in the entire time'; the first requires the whole lifetime, the second a part.
This qiyas is used to support Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If husband says 'in tomorrow' and intends the end of the day, Abu Hanifa accepts that in court; the Sahibayn do not (only in conscience).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما إذا استعملت في الزمان بأن يقول: أنت طالق غداً، فقال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله: يستوي في ذلك حذفها أو إظهارها، حتى لو قال: أنت طالق في غد كان بمنزلة قوله: أنت طالق غداً يقع الطلاق كما طلع الفجر في الصورتين جميعاً. وذهب أبو حنيفة رحمه الله إلى أنها إذا حذفت يقع الطلاق كما طلع الفجر، وإذا أظهرت كان المراد وقوع الطلاق في جزء من الغد على سبيل الإبهام، فلولا وجود النية يقع الطلاق في جزء من الغد. مثال: أن تقول: أنت طالق غداً يعني اختلفوا في حذف "في" وإثباته أيهما يقتضي استيعاب مدخول "في" حتى يكون ما بعد "في" معياراً لما قبله غير فاضل عما قبله، وأيهما لا يقتضيه حتى يكون ما بعد "في" ظرفاً لما قبله فاضلاً عما قبله، فقال الصاحبان: هما سواء في أنه يستوعب جميع ما بعده، فقوله غداً أو قوله في غد سواء في كون الغد معياراً لما بعده، حتى لو قال نويت به أخر النهار لا يصدق قضاء؛ لأنه خلاف الظاهر، فإن الظاهر أن المراد بالغد كله فإذا نوى أخر النهار فقد نوى تخصيص البعض، وهذا خلاف الظاهر بل يصدق فيهما ديانة؛ لأنه نوى محتمل كلامه. وأما عند أبي حنيفة إذا حذفت "في" واتصل الفعل بالظرف بأن قال: أنت طالق غداً، فيراد به الاستيعاب إن أمكن؛ لأنه حينئذ شابه المفعول به حيث انتصب بالفعل، فيقتضي الاستيعاب كالمفعول به يقتضي تعلق الفعل بمجموعه إن أمكن فإذا قال نويت آخر النهار لا يصدق قضاء؛ لأنه غير موجب كلامه، فلابد أن يقع الطلاق في أول النهار. وأما إذا اتصل الفعل به بواسطة "في" اقتضى وقوعه في جزء من النهار؛ إذ ليس من ضرورة الظرفية الاستيعاب فإذا قال: في غد، وقال: أردت آخر النهار يصدق قضاء كما يصدق ديانة؛ لوقوعه في جزء مبهم من الغد، وله ولاية التعيين. ونظير هذا: لأصومن الدهر وفي الدهر، فإن الأول يقتضي استيعاب العمر، بخلاف الثاني؛ فإنه يقع على الساحة كذا قال فخر الإسلام.
As for when it is used in time, such as saying 'You are divorced tomorrow,' Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: In this case, omitting it or mentioning it is equal, so that if he says 'You are divorced in tomorrow' it is equivalent to his saying 'You are divorced tomorrow,' the divorce occurs at dawn in both cases. Abu Hanifa held that if it is omitted, the divorce occurs at dawn, and if it is mentioned, the intended meaning is the occurrence of divorce in a part of tomorrow in an ambiguous way, so if there is no intention, the divorce occurs in a part of tomorrow. Example: You say 'You are divorced tomorrow' means they differed about omitting 'في' and affirming it, as to which implies the encompassment of the object of 'في' so that what follows 'في' is a standard for what precedes it without excess, and which does not imply it so that what follows 'في' is a container for what precedes it and exceeds it. The two companions said: They are equal in that it encompasses all that follows, so his saying 'tomorrow' or 'in tomorrow' are equal regarding tomorrow being a standard for what follows, so that if he says 'I intended the end of the day' it is not accepted in court because it contradicts the apparent meaning; the apparent meaning is that the whole of tomorrow is intended, so if he intends the end of the day, he has intended particularization of a part, which contradicts the apparent. Rather, it is accepted in both cases regarding inner conscience because he intended what is possible in his speech. According to Abu Hanifa: If 'في' is omitted and the verb is directly connected to the adverbial, like 'You are divorced tomorrow,' it indicates encompassment if possible, because then it resembles the direct object since it is in the accusative case due to the verb, so it necessitates encompassment just as the direct object necessitates the verb's attachment to the whole if possible. So if he says 'I intended the end of the day,' it is not accepted in court because it does not necessitate his speech; rather, the divorce must occur at the beginning of the day. If the verb is connected to it by means of 'في,' it necessitates its occurrence in a part of the day, since it is not necessary for adverbiality to encompass. So if he says 'in tomorrow' and says 'I intended the end of the day,' it is accepted in court just as it is accepted in inner conscience, because it occurs in an ambiguous part of tomorrow, and he has the authority to specify. An analogy is: 'I will fast the entire time' and 'I will fast in the entire time'; the first requires encompassing the entire lifetime, unlike the second, for it occurs in a stretch, as said by Fakhr al-Islam.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage discusses the interpretation of the word 'في' in temporal contexts, specifically in divorce pronouncements. The dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn centers on whether the presence of 'في' (in) affects the scope of the time word. When a husband says 'You are divorced tomorrow' (without 'في'), Abu Hanifa says it implies the entire day, so the divorce occurs at dawn (the first part). If he says 'You are divorced in tomorrow' (with 'في'), it implies an ambiguous part of the day, so the husband can intend a specific part (e.g., the end of the day) and be trusted in court. The Sahibayn say both phrases are equivalent, both enforcing the entire day, and an intention to particularize is not accepted in court but only in conscience. The analogy of fasting 'the entire time' vs. 'in the entire time' illustrates the same principle: without 'في', the action covers the whole period; with 'في', it covers a part.

Key Terms
استيعاب (istīʿāb): Encompassment of the entire duration or object of the adverbial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a husband says 'You are divorced in tomorrow' and later claims he intended the end of the day, what happens?
A) The divorce occurs at dawn regardless.
B) His intention is accepted both in court and conscience.
C) His intention is accepted only in conscience, not in court.
D) The divorce is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The presence or absence of 'في' in a temporal phrase changes the legal implication from full day to ambiguous part, affecting the ruling in divorce and similar acts.

The Preposition 'fi' in Temporal Contexts: Totality vs. Partiality
Analyzing the effect of the preposition 'fi' in temporal phrases on divorce rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that omitting 'fi' from a temporal phrase implies totality (isti'ab) and including it implies only a part, and evaluate the practical consequence in divorce and oath scenarios.

Core Idea
Omitting the preposition 'fi' from a time adverb makes the legal action encompass the whole period; including 'fi' makes it apply to only an ambiguous part.

This lesson examines a subtle but crucial distinction in Hanafi legal interpretation: the effect of the preposition 'في' on temporal phrases. The dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, centers on whether a divorce pronouncement 'in tomorrow' (في غد) implies the entire day or merely a part. Understanding this disagreement reveals how linguistic precision shapes legal outcomes and illustrates the Hanafi use of qiyas (analogy) to the direct object.

Guided Path
1
State the linguistic issue
Identify the core question: Does the presence or absence of the preposition 'في' change the scope of the time period mentioned?
The dispute hinges on whether the adverb 'غد' (tomorrow) when connected directly to the verb or via 'في' implies totality or partiality.
2
Identify the two positions
Differentiate between Abu Hanifa's view (omitting 'في' implies totality; including it implies partiality) and the two companions' view (both forms imply totality).
The two companions treat both constructions as equivalent.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Understand Abu Hanifa's analogy: the direct connection of verb to adverb resembles the direct object (maf'ul bih), which requires the action to affect the whole entity. Including 'في' breaks this direct connection, making the adverb a container (zarf) that only implies a part.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on Arabic grammar.
4
Explore the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the dispute to a concrete scenario: if a husband says 'You are divorced in tomorrow' and later claims he intended the end of the day, Abu Hanifa accepts his claim in court, but the two companions do not.
The practical difference lies in whether the court accepts the husband's specification of a part.
5
Apply the principle to oaths
Extend the rule to other contexts: 'I will fast the month' implies fasting the entire month; 'I will fast in the month' requires only a part, even an hour.
This illustrates the broader application of the linguistic principle.

فصل في كلمة في. أما إذا استُعملت في الزمان بأن يقول: أنت طالق غداً، فقال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله: يستوي في ذلك حذفها أو إظهارها، حتى لو قال: أنت طالق في غد كان بمنزلة قوله: أنت طالق غداً يقع الطلاق كما طلع الفجر في الصورتين جميعاً. وذهب أبو حنيفة رحمه الله إلى أنها إذا حذفت يقع الطلاق كما طلع الفجر، وإذا أظهرت كان المراد وقوع الطلاق في جزء من الغد على سبيل الإبهام، فلولا وجود النية يقع. أما إذا استُعملت إلخ: مثل أن تقول: أنت طالق غداً يعني اختلفوا في حذف في وإثباته بأن أيهما يقتضي استيعاب مدخول في حتى يكون ما بعد في معياراً لما قبله غير فاضل عما قبله، وأيهما لا يقتضيه حتى يكون ما بعد في ظرفاً لما قبله فاضلاً عما قبله، فقال الصاحبان: هما سواء في أنه يستوعب جميع ما بعده، فقوله: غداً، أو قوله: في غد سواء في كون الغد معياراً لما بعده، حتى لو قال نويت به أخر النهار لا يصدق قضاء؛ لأنه خلاف الظاهر، فإن الظاهر أن المراد بالغد كله فإذا نوى أخر النهار فقد نوى تخصيص البعض، وهذا خلاف الظاهر بل يصدق فيهما ديانة؛ لأنه نوى محتمل كلامه، وأما عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله: إذا حذفت في واتصل الفعل بالظرف بأن قال: أنت طالق غداً، فيراد به الاستيعاب إن أمكن؛ لأنه حينئذ شابه المفعول به حيث انتصب بالفعل، فيقتضي الاستيعاب كالمفعول به يقتضي تعلق الفعل بمجموعه إن أمكن فإذا قال نويت آخر النهار لا يصدق قضاء؛ لأنه غير موجب كلامه، فلابد أن يقع الطلاق في أول النهار، وأما إذا اتصل الفعل به بواسطة في اقتضى وقوعه في جزء من النهار؛ إذ ليس من ضرورة الظرفية الاستيعاب فإذا قال: في غد، وقال: أردت آخر النهار يصدق قضاء كما يصدق ديانة؛ لوقوعه في جزء مبهم من الغد، وله ولاية التعيين، ونظير هذا: لأصومن الدهر وفي الدهر، فإن الأول يقتضي استيعاب العمر، بخلاف الثاني؛ فإنه يقع على الساحة كذا قال فخر الإسلام بقوله. كما طلع الفجر إلخ لأنه كلمة في إذا حذفت اتصل الطلاق بالغد بلا واسطة حرف الجر، وهي في، فيقتضي استيعاب الغد بالطلاق، فيكون جميع الغد موقعاً للطلاق، فلابد أن يقع الطلاق في أول الغد ليستوعب الطلاق جميع الغد. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ١٤٨] في جزء من الغد إلخ: وذلك لأنها إذا ذكرت صارت الطلاق مضافاً إلى جزء مبهم من الغد، وذلك لا يقتضي الاستيعاب. الطلاق بأوّل الجزء؛ لعدم المزاحم له، ولو نوى آخر النهار صحت نيته. ومثال ذلك: في قول الرجل: إن صمت الشهر فأنت كذا، فإنه يقع على صوم الشهر، ولو قال: إن صمت في الشهر فأنت كذا يقع ذلك على الإمساك ساعة في الشهر.
Section on the word 'fi'. If it is used in time, such as saying: 'You are divorced tomorrow,' then Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: It is the same whether it is omitted or expressed, so that if he said: 'You are divorced in tomorrow' it is like his saying: 'You are divorced tomorrow'; divorce occurs at dawn in both cases. Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) held that when it is omitted, divorce occurs at dawn, and when it is expressed, the intended meaning is the occurrence of divorce in a part of tomorrow in an ambiguous manner, and if there is no intention it occurs. As for when it is used, etc.: For example, if you say 'You are divorced tomorrow', meaning they differed about omitting and affirming 'fi', as to which requires encompassing the object of 'fi' so that what follows 'fi' becomes a standard for what precedes it without excess, and which does not require it so that what follows 'fi' becomes a container for what precedes it with excess. The two companions said: Both are equal in requiring encompassing of all that follows it, so his saying 'tomorrow' or his saying 'in tomorrow' are equal in making 'tomorrow' a standard for what follows it, so that if he said 'I intended the end of the day' it is not accepted in court because it contradicts the apparent meaning; the apparent meaning is that the whole of tomorrow is intended. If he intended the end of the day, he intended to specify a part, which is contrary to the apparent meaning; rather it is accepted religiously because he intended a possible meaning of his words. According to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him): If 'fi' is omitted and the verb is directly connected to the adverb by saying 'You are divorced tomorrow', then the intended meaning is encompassing if possible, because then it resembles the direct object as it is in the accusative case due to the verb, thus requiring encompassing like the direct object requires the verb to relate to its entirety if possible. So if he said 'I intended the end of the day' it is not accepted in court because it does not necessitate his words; therefore divorce must occur at the beginning of the day. And if the verb is connected to it by means of 'fi', it requires its occurrence in a part of the day, since it is not necessary for adverbiality to require encompassing. So if he says 'in tomorrow' and says 'I intended the end of the day', it is accepted in court as it is accepted religiously, because it occurs in an ambiguous part of tomorrow, and he has the authority to specify. Similar to this is: 'I will fast the whole time' and 'in the whole time', for the first requires encompassing of the life, contrary to the second, for it applies to a surface. Thus said Fakhr al-Islam (may Allah be pleased with him). As the dawn breaks etc. Because the word 'fi' when omitted, the divorce is connected to 'tomorrow' without the intermediary of the preposition 'fi', so it requires encompassing of tomorrow by divorce, so all of tomorrow becomes the locus of divorce, so divorce must occur at the beginning of tomorrow to encompass all of tomorrow. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p.148] In a part of the day etc: That is because when it is mentioned, the divorce becomes attached to an ambiguous part of tomorrow, and that does not require encompassing. Divorce at the first part because there is no competing factor, and if he intended the end of the day his intention is valid. An example: In a man's saying: 'If you fast the month, then you are such-and-such', then it applies to fasting the whole month. And if he said: 'If you fast in the month, then you are such-and-such', it applies to refraining for an hour in the month.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the word 'في' when used in temporal contexts, specifically in divorce and oath expressions. The core issue is whether the preposition 'في' indicates a totality (استيعاب) or merely a partial moment. The scholars differ: the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that omitting or including 'في' makes no difference—both imply totality of the time period mentioned. Therefore, if a man says to his wife 'You are divorced tomorrow' or 'You are divorced in tomorrow', divorce occurs at the beginning of tomorrow. If he later claims he intended the end of the day, this is not accepted in court because it contradicts the apparent meaning, though it may be accepted religiously as a valid intention. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: if 'في' is omitted, the verb connects directly to the adverb (ghad) like a direct object (maf'ul bih), implying totality; if 'في' is included, the verb is connected via a preposition, implying only a part of the time. So in the latter case, the husband's specification of a particular part (e.g., the end of the day) is accepted both in court and religiously, because the phrase is ambiguous. The same principle applies to oaths: 'I will fast the month' requires fasting the entire month, while 'I will fast in the month' only requires fasting any part of it, even an hour.

Key Terms
استيعاب (isti'ab): Totality or encompassing of the entire time or object mentioned.
ظرف (zarf): A container or adverb of time or place; when used with the preposition 'في', it indicates that the action occurs within some part of that container, not necessarily the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this lesson, if a man says to his wife 'أنت طالق في غد' and later claims he intended the divorce to occur at the last moment of tomorrow, what is the ruling in court?
A) The claim is not accepted because the apparent meaning implies totality.
B) The claim is accepted because the preposition 'في' makes the time ambiguous.
C) The claim is accepted only if he has witnesses.
D) The divorce does not occur because the intention contradicts the expression.

Key Takeaway
The presence or absence of the preposition 'في' in temporal phrases determines whether a legal action encompasses the entire time period or only an ambiguous part, a distinction that has direct consequences for divorce and oath rulings in Hanafi law.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Rule of 'في' in Conditional Oaths: Intransitive vs Transitive Actions
Explaining the rule of 'في' when attached to time/place in oaths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for interpreting 'في' in oaths by distinguishing between actions complete with the subject and those requiring an object, using the examples of insult, hitting, and killing.

Core Idea
In oaths, 'في' directs the condition to where the action's effect occurs: subject-place for intransitive, object-place for transitive.

When a person swears an oath and uses the word 'في' (in, during, at) to attach a time or place to the action, the Hanafi school applies a nuanced rule: the location of the condition depends on whether the action is complete with the subject alone or requires an object. This lesson unpacks that rule through vivid examples from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's al-Jami' al-Kabir, showing how the same preposition can shift the ruling based on the verb's transitivity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verb type
Determine whether the action in the oath is intransitive (complete with subject, e.g., insult, fast) or transitive (needs an object, e.g., hit, kill).
For intransitive, the condition attaches to subject's location; for transitive, to the object's location.
2
Analyze the role of 'في'
Recognize that 'في' creates an adverbial (zarf) that specifies the time or place of the action's occurrence. It does not imply continuity or totality.
E.g., 'fast in the month' means only some part, not the whole month.
3
Apply the rule to the examples
Work through the three cases from al-Jami' al-Kabir: insult (intransitive → subject's location), hit/laceration (transitive → object's location), kill (transitive → time of death as effect).
Note the contrast: for insult, only the insulter's presence matters; for hit, only the victim's location matters.
4
Refute the potential counterargument
Consider the objection that since transitive actions need both subject and object, both should be bound by the place. The Hanafi response: the action's identity is determined by its effect on the object, so the place of that effect governs.
The effect (e.g., wound, death) is the essence of the action, not the subject's action alone.
5
Extend to divorce example
Apply the same principle to 'you are divorced in the house': immediate divorce unless an implied action (e.g., entering) is intended, which shifts the interpretation to conditional.
The adverbial interpretation requires 'في' to modify a suitable action; place is not inherently an adverbial for divorce.

الإطلاق أي يكون الطلاق في جميع الأماكن في الحال؛ لأن المكان لا يصلح ظرفاً للطلاق؛ إذ الظرف للشيء بمنزلة الوصف له، وما كان وصفاً للشيء لابد أن يكون صالحاً للتخصيص، والموصوف مختص بالوصف ومسند ،به والمكان لا يصلح للطلاق بحال؛ لأنه إذا وقع في يقع فيه الطلاق إذا أضيف إلى المكان فقيل: أنت طالق في الدار وقع في الحال، إلا أن يراد به إضمار الفعل بأن أريد في دخولك الدار ، فيصير بمعنى الشرط، فلا تطلق في الحال؛ لأنه ذكر المحل وأراد الفعل الحال، فيصدق فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى؛ لأن اللفظ يحتمله ولكنه خلاف الظاهر، فلا يصدق قضاء. يتعدى إلخ: أي يتوقف وجوده إلى مفعول كالضرب والشج والقتل مثلاً، فإنهما لا تتم بوجود الفاعل وحده بل يتوقف على وجود المفعول، وهو المضروب والمشجوج والمقتول. مكان لأن الفعل إنما يَتَحَقَّقُ بأَثره وأَثَرُهُ في المَحَلِّ قال محمد يحلله في "الجامع الكبير": إذا قال: "إن شَتَمتُكَ في المسجد فكذا"، فشَتَمَهُ وهو في المسجد، والمشتوم خارج المسجد يحنث، ولو كان الشاتم خارج المسجد والمشتوم في المسجد لا يحنث. ولو قال: "إن ضربتك أو شجَتُك في المسجد فكذا" يشترط كون المضروب والمشجوج في المسجد، ولا يشترط كون الضارب والشاج فيه. ولو قال: "إن قَتَلْتُكَ في يوم الخميس "فكذا فجرحه قبل يوم الخميس ومات يوم الخميس يحنث، ولو جرحه يوم الخميس ومات يوم الجمعة لا يحنَتُ. لأن الفعل إنما إلخ لأن الأفعال إنما تعرف بظهور آثارها في محلها ألا ترى أنه تختلف أسماءها باختلاف آثارها، فإن من أرسل خشبة من الأعلى على غيره، فإن أثره في الإيلام يسمى ضرباً، وإن أثره في الجرح يسمى جرحاً، وإن أثره في إزهاق الروح يسمى قتلاً، ولما اختلف الفعل باختلاف آثارها علمنا أن اسم الفعل باعتبار ما ثبت بالمفعول به فيراعي المكان في حقه، ونحن نقول بهذا الاستدلال خرج الجواب عما قيل: إن هذه الأفعال تتم بالفاعل والمفعول لا بأحدهما، فيجب أن يراعي المكان في حقهما؛ لأن الفعل لم يثبت إلا لمعنى اختص بالمفعول وهو أثر الفعل، وهذا توضيح ما في "المعدن". وأَثَرُهُ فِي المَحَلّ: أي في محل يقع عليه فيراعي المكان والزمان في حق المحل كذا في "المعدن". يحنث: لأن الشتم يتم بالشاتم ،وحده، فكان شرط الحنث وجوده في المسجد وقد وجد كذا قيل لا يحنث: وهذا مشكل؛ لأن تحققه كما يكون بما يؤثر فيه يكون بالمؤثر أيضاً، فكلاهما مما يتوقف عليه الفعل، واشتراط الظرفية في أحدهما دون الآخر تحكم؛ لأنا نقول: لما كان الفعل متعدياً وذكر المحل مع الفاعل يكون المقصود وقوع الفاعل على المحل ضرورة، ويكون المحل هو المقصود، فاشتراط الظرفية في المحل لهذا كما في "مفتاح العلوم". يشترط كون المضروب إلخ لأن الضرب والشج لا يتمان بالفاعل وحده، بل يتوقف على وجود المضروب والمشحوج أيضاً، فكان شرط الحنث وجودهما في المسجد. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ١٥٠] يحنَثُ: أي الحالف المتكلم بوجود الشرط وهو القتل في يوم الخميس؛ لأن القتل إنما يصير قتلاً عند زهوق الروح، ألا ترى أنه قبل زهوق الروح في يوم الخميس يسمى جرحاً، وبعد زهوق الروح يسمى قتلاً، فيراعي زمان زهوق الروح، و لم يوجد زهوق الروح في يوم الخميس، فلم يوجد شرط الحنث وهو القتل فيه كذا قيل.
The first investigation in the Book of Allah. Chapter on the word 'في'. Divorce at the first part of the day because there is no competitor. If he intended the end of the day, his intention is valid. An example: a man saying, 'If I fast the month, then you are such-and-such'—it applies to fasting the entire month. If he says, 'If I fast in the month, then you are such-and-such'—it applies to refraining for an hour in the month. Added divorce: Regarding place, like his saying, 'You are divorced in the house, and in Mecca'—that is divorce absolutely in all places. Considering the adverbial sense, we say: if he swears an oath on an action and attaches it to a time or place, then if the action is complete with the subject, the condition requires the subject to be in that time or place; if the action is transitive to a location, the condition requires the location to be in that time or place. His intention is valid because he specifies one of its probabilities without changing its requirement. When the word 'في' appears, what enters upon 'في' becomes purely adverbial. The adverbial of divorce is only in a part of the next day, and that does not necessitate continuity. 'Applies to fasting' etc.: The condition of his breaking the oath is fasting the entire month without the preposition, thus it requires covering the month with fasting. 'Applies to that' etc.: Because the action is attached to an undefined part of the month, and that does not require continuity. 'In all places' etc.: A substitution for his saying 'absolutely', i.e., the divorce occurs in all places immediately, because place is not suitable as an adverbial for divorce; the adverbial for a thing is like a description of it, and a description must be suitable for specification, and the described is associated with the description. Place is not suitable for divorce at all; because if divorce is added to a place, like 'You are divorced in the house', it occurs immediately, unless the action is implied, meaning 'in your entering the house'—then it becomes conditional, so she is not divorced immediately; he mentioned the location and intended the action occurring, so he is truthful between himself and Allah because the wording bears it, but it contradicts the apparent meaning, so he is not believed in court. 'Transitive' etc.: Its existence requires an object, like hitting, laceration, and killing; these are not completed by the subject alone but depend on the existence of the object—the one hit, lacerated, or killed. Place. Because the action is only realized by its effect, and its effect is in the location. Muhammad (al-Shaybani) analyzes in 'al-Jami' al-Kabir': If he says, 'If I insult you in the mosque, then such-and-such', and he insults him while the insulter is in the mosque and the insulted is outside the mosque, he breaks the oath; if the insulter is outside and the insulted inside, he does not break. If he says, 'If I hit you or lacerate you in the mosque, then such-and-such', it is required that the one hit or lacerated be in the mosque, and it is not required that the hitter or lasher be in it. If he says, 'If I kill you on Thursday, then such-and-such', and he wounds him before Thursday and he dies on Thursday, he breaks the oath; if he wounds him on Thursday and he dies on Friday, he does not break. 'Because the action only' etc.: Actions are only known by the appearance of their effects in their locations. Do you not see that their names differ according to their effects? If one sends a piece of wood from above onto another, if its effect is pain, it is called hitting; if its effect is wounding, it is called laceration; if its effect is causing death, it is called killing. Since actions differ by their effects, we know that the name of the action is based on what is established in the object, so place is considered concerning it. We say by this inference the answer emerges to what is said: These actions are completed by the subject and object, not by one of them, so place should be considered concerning both. Because the action is only established for a meaning specific to the object—the effect of the action. This clarifies what is in 'al-Ma'din'. 'And its effect in the location': i.e., in the location upon which it falls, so place and time are considered concerning the location, as in 'al-Ma'din'. 'He breaks the oath': because insult is completed by the insulter alone, so the condition of breaking was his presence in the mosque, and he was present. It is said that he does not break; this is problematic because its realization is as much by what affects as by the effecter, so both depend on the action. Specifying the adverbial for one without the other is arbitrary. We say: since the action is transitive and the location is mentioned with the subject, the intended meaning is necessarily the occurrence of the subject upon the location, and the location is the intended object. So the adverbial is specified for the location for this reason, as in 'Miftah al-Ulum'. 'It is required that the one hit etc.': because hitting and laceration are not completed by the subject alone, but depend on the existence of the one hit and lacerated, so the condition of breaking is their presence in the mosque. [from 'Umdat al-Hawashi, p. 150] 'He breaks': i.e., the one who swore the oath concerning the existence of the condition—killing on Thursday. Because killing only becomes killing when the soul departs. Do you not see that before the soul departs on Thursday it is called wounding, and after the soul departs it is called killing? So the time of the soul's departure is considered, and the soul's departure did not occur on Thursday, so the condition of the oath—killing on it—did not occur. As it is said.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rule governing the word 'في' (in, during, at) when it appears in conditional oaths. The author explains that when a person swears an oath and attaches the action to a time or place using 'في', the interpretation depends on the nature of the action. If the action is complete with the subject alone (intransitive, like fast or divorce), then the condition for breaking the oath is that the subject must be present in that time or place. If the action requires an object (transitive, like hitting or killing), then the condition is about the location of the object, not the subject. The text illustrates this with examples: in divorce, saying 'You are divorced in the house' causes immediate divorce unless the speaker intended an implied action (e.g., 'in entering the house'), which is truthful between him and Allah but not in court. In fasting, saying 'If I fast in the month' means only one hour, while 'If I fast the month' requires the whole month. The commentary then cites Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's 'al-Jami' al-Kabir' for three cases: insult (intransitive—dependent on the insulter's location), hitting/laceration (transitive—dependent on the victim's location), and killing (transitive—the killing is only considered when the soul departs, so time is tied to the death moment). The rationale is that actions are known by their effects on the object; the effect determines the name of the action. The discussion refutes an opposing view that both subject and object should be considered equally, arguing that the action's essence lies in its effect on the object.

Key Terms
في (fi): A preposition (harf jar) meaning 'in', 'during', or 'at', used to attach an action to a time or place in a conditional oath.
الظرفية (al-zarfiyya): The quality of being an adverbial (zarf) of time or place; the sense of 'in which' something occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone swears saying, 'If I insult you in the mosque', when does he break his oath?
A) When the insulter is in the mosque, regardless of the location of the insulted.
B) When the insulted is in the mosque, regardless of the location of the insulter.
C) When both the insulter and the insulted are in the mosque.
D) Only if the insult occurs exactly at the mosque's door.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the interpretation of 'في' in oaths hinges on the transitivity of the verb: intransitive conditions attach to the subject, transitive conditions attach to the location of the effect on the object.

Particle 'Fi' with Verbs: From Container to Condition
Showing that 'fi' on verbs indicates condition due to impossibility of literal reading.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the particle 'fi' indicates a condition rather than a container in oath/divorce contexts, and apply the Hanafi usul principle of shifting from literal to figurative meaning when literal is impossible.

Core Idea
When literal meaning is impossible, particles shift to condition due to association.

In Hanafi usul, words are interpreted according to their literal meaning unless that meaning is impossible. When the particle 'fi' (in) is attached to a verbal noun, the literal sense of containment is impossible because actions are transient accidents. The particle then takes on the meaning of a condition (shart). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this shift and shows how it applies to real cases of divorce oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle and its literal sense
Recognize that 'fi' literally means 'in' (container). With nouns, it works; with verbs, it cannot because verbs are actions that don't persist.
2
Check possibility of literal reading
Ask: can the verbal noun serve as a container for the legal effect? Since verbs are accidents (a'rad) lasting only an instant, they cannot contain anything.
Divorce is a legal consequence; it cannot be 'inside' an action.
3
Identify the nearest possible meaning
When literal is impossible, move to the next plausible meaning by analogy. Between container (zarf) and condition (shart) there is association: both involve a relation of accompaniment.
Hence 'fi' is interpreted as 'with' (ma'a), which then functions as a condition.
4
Apply to examples
Work through the given cases: 'You are divorced upon your entering the house' means divorce occurs when entering occurs; 'upon the coming of the day' means at dawn; 'upon the passing of the day' means after a full day.
The condition must be clearly definable (e.g., entering, menstruation, day passage).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو دخلت الكلمة في الفعل تفيد معنى الشرط.
قال محمد محله: إذا قال: "أنت طالق في دخولك الدار" فهو بمعنى الشرط، فلا يقع الطلاق قبل دخول الدار. ولو قال: أنت طالق في حيضتك" إن كانت في الحيض وقع الطلاق في الحال وإلا يتعلق الطلاق بالحيض.
لوجود الشرط في الحال
وفي "الجامع": لو قال: "أنت طالق في مجيء يوم" لم تُطلق حتى يطلع الفجر. ولو قال: "في مُضي يوم" إن كان ذلك في الليل وقع الطلاق عند غروب الشمس من الغد لوجود الشرط، وإن كان في اليوم تطلقُ حين تجيء من الغد تلك الساعة.
وهو معنى اليوم ذلك الكلام
تفيد معنى الشرط: لأن الفعل كالدخول والخروج لا يصلح ظرفاً للطلاق على معنى أن يكون شاملاً له؛ لأنه عرض لا يبقى زمانين، والظرف محل للمظروف وما لا يبقى زمانين لا يكون محل الشيء، فإذا تعذرت الحقيقة وهي الظرفية حمل على الشرط مجازاً؛ لما أن بين الشرط والظرف مقارنة.
بمعنى الشرط إلخ لأن الأقوال لا تصلح ظرفاً للطلاق على معنى أن يكون شاملاً؛ لأنه عرض لا يبقى زمانين، والظرف محل للمظروف، وما لا يبقى زمانين لا يكون محل الشيء، ولكن بين الظرف والشرط مناسبة من حيث المقارنة؛ لما أن بين الظرف والمظروف مقارنة كما بين الشرط والمشروط، فحمل "على" بمعنى "مع"، فإن حرف الصلوة يقام بعضها مقام البعض بدليل أنه لو قال مع دخولك الدار يقع الطلاق كذا في "المعدن". حتى يطلع الفجر لأن اليوم من طلوع الفجر إلى غروب الشمس، بخلاف النهار؛ فإنه من طلوعها إلى غروبها، وفي بعض النسخ: حتى تطلع الشمس، وهو غير صواب كما لا يخفى عند غروب الشمس: لأن الطلاق معلق بعضي ،اليوم، وذا إنما يوجد إذا مضى جميع ساعات اليوم، ومضي جميع الساعات إنما يكون عند غروب الشمس الغد إذا قال هذا الكلام في الليل، وعند مجيء تلك الساعة التي وجد الكلام فيها إذا كان هذا القول في اليوم. حين تجيء من الغد يعني: إذا حلف وقت الزوال يقع الطلاق إذا جاء وقت الزوال من الغد؛ لأن الشرط مضي يوم كامل، فإذا مضى نصف النهار في يوم الحلف والنصف الثاني من الغد كان اليوم كاملاً، فوقع الطلاق لوجود الشرط كذا في "المعدن".
And if the word (fi) enters the verb, it conveys the meaning of a condition. Muhammad (al-Shaybani) said, in his place: If he says, 'You are divorced upon your entering the house,' it is in the meaning of a condition, so divorce does not occur before entering the house. And if he said, 'You are divorced during your menstruation,' if she was in menstruation, divorce occurs immediately; otherwise, divorce is attached to menstruation. (Because the condition exists immediately.) And in al-Jami': If he said, 'You are divorced upon the coming of the day,' she is not divorced until dawn breaks. And if he said, 'Upon the passing of the day,' if that was at night, divorce occurs at sunset of the next day due to the existence of the condition; if it was during the day, she is divorced when that same hour comes the next day. (And that is the meaning of 'day' in that statement.) 'It conveys the meaning of a condition': because verbs like entering and exiting are not suitable as containers for divorce in the sense of encompassing it; because they are accidents that do not persist for two moments, and the container is a locus for the contained, and what does not persist for two moments cannot be a locus for a thing. So when the literal meaning (being a container) is impossible, it is carried metaphorically to a condition, due to the association between condition and container. 'In the meaning of a condition, etc.': because utterances are not suitable as containers for divorce in the sense of encompassing; because it is an accident that does not persist for two moments, and the container is a locus for the contained, and what does not persist for two moments cannot be a locus for a thing. But there is a suitability between container and condition in terms of association; because there is an association between container and contained just as between condition and conditioned. So it (the particle) is interpreted as 'with'; for particles can take the place of one another, as evidenced by the fact that if he said 'with your entering the house,' divorce occurs. This is in al-Ma'din. 'Until dawn breaks': because the day is from dawn to sunset, unlike the daytime (nahar), which is from sunrise to sunset. In some copies: 'until the sun rises,' which is incorrect as is clear. 'At sunset': because divorce is suspended on the passing of the day, and that only occurs if all hours of the day have passed, and the passing of all hours is at sunset of the next day if he said this statement at night, and at the coming of that hour in which the statement occurred if the statement was during the day. 'When that same hour comes the next day': meaning, if he swore at noon, divorce occurs when noon comes the next day; because the condition is the passing of a complete day. So if half the day passed on the day of the oath and the second half the next day, the day is complete, so divorce occurs due to the existence of the condition. This is in al-Ma'din.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage explains that when the particle 'fi' (in/upon) is attached to a verbal noun (like 'entering', 'passing'), it does not function literally as a container (zarf) because actions are transient accidents. Instead, it is interpreted as a condition (shart). The author cites Imam Muhammad's examples: 'You are divorced upon your entering the house' means divorce occurs when the condition of entering is met, not before. If said during menstruation, divorce is immediate if she is already menstruating; otherwise, it attaches to the future menstruation. Further examples from al-Jami' clarify timing: 'upon the coming of the day' means at dawn; 'upon the passing of the day' means after a full day passes from the statement. The reasoning is that verbs cannot be containers for the effect (divorce) because they are non-enduring, so the particle is reinterpreted conjunctively as 'with' (ma'a), which is analogous to condition. This is a Hanafi usul principle that prioritizes meaningful interpretation over literal reading when literal meaning is impossible.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition that must be fulfilled for a legal consequence (e.g., divorce) to occur.
ظرف (zarf): A container or adverbial of place/time; literally 'in'.
فعل (fi'l): Verb; here specifically a verbal noun (masdar) denoting an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Immediately at the time of utterance.
B) At the next dawn.
C) At sunset the next day.
D) At the same hour the next night.

Key Takeaway
When 'fi' enters a verb in a legal context, Hanafi usul interprets it as a condition, not a container, due to the impossibility of an action serving as a locus.

Bayan al-Taqrir and Bayan al-Tafsir: Confirmation and Interpretation
Defines and exemplifies the first two types of bayan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Bayan al-Taqrir from Bayan al-Tafsir and apply the ruling of validity for connected and disconnected clarifications.

Core Idea
Bayan al-Taqrir confirms the apparent meaning; Bayan al-Tafsir reveals the unclear — both are valid whether connected or disconnected.

In Hanafi usul, when we encounter a legal text, we need to know how it is clarified. Imam al-Shashi categorizes clarification (bayan) into types based on the nature of the original text. This lesson focuses on the first two: confirmation (taqrir) and interpretation (tafsir). You will learn to identify each type and understand its ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of ambiguity
Determine if the original word is apparent but has a remote possibility (taqrir) or unclear/unexplained (tafsir).
If the word is clear but could be interpreted otherwise, it's taqrir. If it's ambiguous, it's tafsir.
2
Match the bayan to the ambiguity
If the clarification simply confirms the apparent meaning, it's taqrir; if it specifies an unclear term, it's tafsir.
3
Apply the ruling
Both are valid whether the clarification is attached (muttasil) or separate (munfasil) from the original statement.
This ruling is explicitly stated in the passage.
4
Work through examples
Practice identifying taqrir vs tafsir in given statements from the text.
Examples include 'qafiz of wheat' (taqrir) and 'something' (tafsir).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في وجوه البيان
البحث الأول في كتاب الله
٤ - وبيان ضرورة ٥- وبيان حال ٦- وبيان عطف ٧- وبيان تبديل. أما الأول: فهو أن يكون معنى اللفظ ظاهراً لكنَّه يحتمل غيره، فبين المراد بما هو الظاهر، أي بيان تقرير. فيتقرر حكم الظاهر ببيانه. ومثاله: إذا قال: "لفلان عليَّ قفيز حنطة بقفيز البلد، أو ألف من نقد البلد"، فإنه يكون بيان تقرير؛ لأن المطلق كان محمولاً على قفيز البلد ونقده مع احتمال إرادة الغير، فإذا بين ذلك فقد قرره ببيانه.
وأما بيان التفسير فهو ما إذا كان اللفظ غير مكشوف المراد فكشفه ببيانه. مثاله: إذا قال: "لفلان علي شيء" ثم فسر الشيء بثوب، أو قال: "علي عشرة دراهم ونيف" ثم فسر النيف، أو قال: "علي دراهم" وفسرها بعشرة مثلاً. وحكم هذين النوعين من البيان: أن يصح موصولاً ومفصولاً.
فصل في بيان التغيير:
وأما بيان التغيير فهو أن يتغير ببيانه معنى كلامه. مثاله: [؟]... 
ثم اعلم أن كونه على سبعة أنواع بالاستقراء على التقريب، وإلا فالتقسيم لا يأبى الزيادة، ووجه الحصر: أن البيان لا يخلو إما أن يكون من المنطوق أو لا، والأول إما أن يكون بياناً لمعنى الكلام أو لازمه كالمدة، الثاني بيان التبديل وهو النسخ، والأول إما أن يكون بلا تغير أو معه، الثاني بيان التغيير كالاستثناء والشرط والغاية، والأول إما أن يكون معنى الكلام معلوماً لكن الثاني أكده بما يقطع الاحتمال أو مجهولاً كالمشترك والمجمل، الثاني بيان التفسير والأول بيان تقرير، والثاني لا يخلو إما أن يكون لمحض السكوت أو لا، الثاني بيان الضرورة، والأول إما أن يكون بدلالة حال المتكلم أو لكثرة الكلام، الأول بيان الحال والثاني بيان العطف كذا قيل.
Chapter on the types of Bayan. First investigation in the Book of Allah. 4- Bayan of necessity, 5- Bayan of state, 6- Bayan of conjunction, 7- Bayan of substitution. As for the first: it is that the meaning of the word is apparent but it admits another possibility, so the intended meaning is clarified by what is apparent, i.e., Bayan al-Taqrir. Thus the ruling of the apparent is confirmed by its clarification. Example: If someone says, 'I owe so-and-so a qafiz of wheat according to the qafiz of the country, or a thousand of the currency of the country,' then it is Bayan al-Taqrir because the absolute was carried on the qafiz of the country and its currency with the possibility of intending something else, so when he clarifies that, he confirms it by his clarification. As for Bayan al-Tafsir: it is when the word is not clear in meaning, so he uncovers it by his clarification. Example: If someone says, 'I owe so-and-so something,' then he interprets 'something' as a garment; or says, 'I owe ten dirhams and some more (nif),' then he interprets the nif; or says, 'I owe dirhams,' and interprets them as ten, etc. The ruling of these two types of Bayan is that they are valid whether connected or disconnected. Chapter on Bayan al-Taghyir: As for Bayan al-Taghyir: it is that the meaning of his speech changes by its clarification. Example: [...] Then know that it is of seven types by approximate induction, otherwise the division does not preclude increase. The reasoning for limitation: Bayan is either from the uttered or not; the first is either a clarification of the meaning of the speech or its implication like the duration, the second is Bayan of substitution (i.e., abrogation); the first is either without change or with change, the second is Bayan of change (like exception, condition, and limit); the first is either that the meaning of the speech is known but the second emphasizes it by cutting off possibility, or unknown like the common and the ambiguous, the second is Bayan of interpretation and the first is Bayan of confirmation; the second is either for pure silence or not, the second is Bayan of necessity; the first is either by indication of the speaker's state or by frequency of speech, the first is Bayan of state and the second is Bayan of conjunction, as it is said.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage defines the seven types of Bayan (clarification) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, particularly as applied to the Quran. The author begins by listing seven types: Bayan al-Taqrir (confirmation), Bayan al-Tafsir (interpretation), Bayan al-Taghyir (change), Bayan al-Darura (necessity), Bayan al-Hal (state), Bayan al-'Atf (conjunction), and Bayan al-Tabdil (substitution/abrogation). The first type, Bayan al-Taqrir, occurs when a word is apparent in meaning but still admits a remote possibility; the speaker then clarifies that the apparent meaning is intended, thus confirming it. For example, if someone says 'a qafiz of wheat according to the qafiz of the country,' the absolute expression defaults to the customary measure, but the clarification removes any doubt. The second type, Bayan al-Tafsir, applies when the word is unclear (mujmal or mushtarak); the speaker then explains its intended meaning, such as explaining 'something' as 'a garment' or adding the specific number after 'dirhams.' Both Bayan al-Taqrir and Bayan al-Tafsir are valid whether they are connected (mutassil) or disconnected (munfasil) from the original statement. The third type, Bayan al-Taghyir, changes the meaning, such as exception or condition. The passage then provides a logical division of all seven types: Bayan is either from the uttered (mantooq) or not; if from the uttered, it either clarifies the meaning itself or its implication (like duration, leading to abrogation); if from the meaning, it either does not change the meaning (Bayan al-Taqrir and Bayan al-Tafsir) or changes it (Bayan al-Taghyir like exception/condition/limit); further subdivisions lead to the other types. This classification is based on induction and is not exhaustive. The author presents this as a clear way to understand how the Quranic text is clarified.

Key Terms
بيان (bayan): Clarification or explanation of a legal text to remove ambiguity or confirm an apparent meaning.
بيان تقرير (bayan al-taqrir): Clarification that confirms the apparent meaning of a word, removing any remote probability of a different interpretation.
بيان تفسير (bayan al-tafsir): Clarification that explains an ambiguous or unclear word (mujmal or mushtarak) by specifying its intended meaning.
بيان تغيير (bayan al-taghyir): Clarification that changes the meaning of the original statement, such as through exception, condition, or limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of Bayan al-Tafsir?
A) A person says 'I owe you a thousand of the country's currency' and then says 'I meant the silver dirhams.'
B) A person says 'I owe you something' and later says 'I meant a camel.'
C) A person says 'I give you this house' and later adds 'except the kitchen.'
D) A person says 'I sell you this car' and later clarifies 'the red one.'

Key Takeaway
Bayan al-Taqrir confirms the apparent meaning; Bayan al-Tafsir reveals the unclear; both are valid whether connected or disconnected to the original text.

The Logical Division of the Seven Types of Bayan
Logical derivation of all seven types of bayan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reproduce the logical division of the seven types of bayan and identify the category of a given clarification.

Core Idea
Bayan is divided by logic into seven types, from mantuq to ghayr mantuq, and from meaning to implication, revealing the systematic nature of Quranic clarification.

In the second part of this passage, Imam al-Shashi presents a logical tree (shajara) that derives all seven types of bayan from first principles. You will learn how each type emerges from dichotomies like mantuq vs. ghayr mantuq, change vs. no change, etc. This systematic approach helps ensure no type is overlooked and shows the depth of Hanafi usul methodology.

Guided Path
1
Start with the dichotomy: bayan from mantuq or from ghayr mantuq
The author first splits bayan into whether it comes from the spoken words (mantooq) or from external indications (ghayr mantooq).
Ghayr mantooq includes types like darura, hal, atf, and tabdil.
2
If from mantuq, further split: bayan of meaning or bayan of implication
From mantooq, bayan either clarifies the meaning of the speech itself or its implication (like duration). The latter leads to abrogation (tabdil).
3
Within the meaning branch, split: bayan with change or without change
Without change gives taqrir and tafsir; with change gives taghyir (exception, condition, limit).
4
Within the no-change branch, split: known meaning with remote possibility vs. unknown meaning
Known meaning with remote possibility = taqrir; unknown meaning = tafsir.
This completes the three main types.
5
Trace the remaining types from the other branches
From ghayr mantooq we get darura, hal, atf. From the implication branch we get tabdil. Follow the text's logic to locate each.
The passage ends with 'as it is said' indicating this is a standard division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في وجوه البيان
البحث الأول في كتاب الله
٤ - وبيان ضرورة ٥- وبيان حال ٦- وبيان عطف ٧- وبيان تبديل. أما الأول: فهو أن يكون معنى اللفظ ظاهراً لكنَّه يحتمل غيره، فبين المراد بما هو الظاهر، أي بيان تقرير. فيتقرر حكم الظاهر ببيانه. ومثاله: إذا قال: "لفلان عليَّ قفيز حنطة بقفيز البلد، أو ألف من نقد البلد"، فإنه يكون بيان تقرير؛ لأن المطلق كان محمولاً على قفيز البلد ونقده مع احتمال إرادة الغير، فإذا بين ذلك فقد قرره ببيانه.
وأما بيان التفسير فهو ما إذا كان اللفظ غير مكشوف المراد فكشفه ببيانه. مثاله: إذا قال: "لفلان علي شيء" ثم فسر الشيء بثوب، أو قال: "علي عشرة دراهم ونيف" ثم فسر النيف، أو قال: "علي دراهم" وفسرها بعشرة مثلاً. وحكم هذين النوعين من البيان: أن يصح موصولاً ومفصولاً.
فصل في بيان التغيير:
وأما بيان التغيير فهو أن يتغير ببيانه معنى كلامه. مثاله: [؟]... 
ثم اعلم أن كونه على سبعة أنواع بالاستقراء على التقريب، وإلا فالتقسيم لا يأبى الزيادة، ووجه الحصر: أن البيان لا يخلو إما أن يكون من المنطوق أو لا، والأول إما أن يكون بياناً لمعنى الكلام أو لازمه كالمدة، الثاني بيان التبديل وهو النسخ، والأول إما أن يكون بلا تغير أو معه، الثاني بيان التغيير كالاستثناء والشرط والغاية، والأول إما أن يكون معنى الكلام معلوماً لكن الثاني أكده بما يقطع الاحتمال أو مجهولاً كالمشترك والمجمل، الثاني بيان التفسير والأول بيان تقرير، والثاني لا يخلو إما أن يكون لمحض السكوت أو لا، الثاني بيان الضرورة، والأول إما أن يكون بدلالة حال المتكلم أو لكثرة الكلام، الأول بيان الحال والثاني بيان العطف كذا قيل.
Chapter on the types of Bayan. First investigation in the Book of Allah. 4- Bayan of necessity, 5- Bayan of state, 6- Bayan of conjunction, 7- Bayan of substitution. As for the first: it is that the meaning of the word is apparent but it admits another possibility, so the intended meaning is clarified by what is apparent, i.e., Bayan al-Taqrir. Thus the ruling of the apparent is confirmed by its clarification. Example: If someone says, 'I owe so-and-so a qafiz of wheat according to the qafiz of the country, or a thousand of the currency of the country,' then it is Bayan al-Taqrir because the absolute was carried on the qafiz of the country and its currency with the possibility of intending something else, so when he clarifies that, he confirms it by his clarification. As for Bayan al-Tafsir: it is when the word is not clear in meaning, so he uncovers it by his clarification. Example: If someone says, 'I owe so-and-so something,' then he interprets 'something' as a garment; or says, 'I owe ten dirhams and some more (nif),' then he interprets the nif; or says, 'I owe dirhams,' and interprets them as ten, etc. The ruling of these two types of Bayan is that they are valid whether connected or disconnected. Chapter on Bayan al-Taghyir: As for Bayan al-Taghyir: it is that the meaning of his speech changes by its clarification. Example: [...] Then know that it is of seven types by approximate induction, otherwise the division does not preclude increase. The reasoning for limitation: Bayan is either from the uttered or not; the first is either a clarification of the meaning of the speech or its implication like the duration, the second is Bayan of substitution (i.e., abrogation); the first is either without change or with change, the second is Bayan of change (like exception, condition, and limit); the first is either that the meaning of the speech is known but the second emphasizes it by cutting off possibility, or unknown like the common and the ambiguous, the second is Bayan of interpretation and the first is Bayan of confirmation; the second is either for pure silence or not, the second is Bayan of necessity; the first is either by indication of the speaker's state or by frequency of speech, the first is Bayan of state and the second is Bayan of conjunction, as it is said.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage defines the seven types of Bayan (clarification) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, particularly as applied to the Quran. The author begins by listing seven types: Bayan al-Taqrir (confirmation), Bayan al-Tafsir (interpretation), Bayan al-Taghyir (change), Bayan al-Darura (necessity), Bayan al-Hal (state), Bayan al-'Atf (conjunction), and Bayan al-Tabdil (substitution/abrogation). The first type, Bayan al-Taqrir, occurs when a word is apparent in meaning but still admits a remote possibility; the speaker then clarifies that the apparent meaning is intended, thus confirming it. For example, if someone says 'a qafiz of wheat according to the qafiz of the country,' the absolute expression defaults to the customary measure, but the clarification removes any doubt. The second type, Bayan al-Tafsir, applies when the word is unclear (mujmal or mushtarak); the speaker then explains its intended meaning, such as explaining 'something' as 'a garment' or adding the specific number after 'dirhams.' Both Bayan al-Taqrir and Bayan al-Tafsir are valid whether they are connected (mutassil) or disconnected (munfasil) from the original statement. The third type, Bayan al-Taghyir, changes the meaning, such as exception or condition. The passage then provides a logical division of all seven types: Bayan is either from the uttered (mantooq) or not; if from the uttered, it either clarifies the meaning itself or its implication (like duration, leading to abrogation); if from the meaning, it either does not change the meaning (Bayan al-Taqrir and Bayan al-Tafsir) or changes it (Bayan al-Taghyir like exception/condition/limit); further subdivisions lead to the other types. This classification is based on induction and is not exhaustive. The author presents this as a clear way to understand how the Quranic text is clarified.

Key Terms
بيان (bayan): Clarification or explanation of a legal text to remove ambiguity or confirm an apparent meaning.
بيان تقرير (bayan al-taqrir): Clarification that confirms the apparent meaning of a word, removing any remote probability of a different interpretation.
بيان تفسير (bayan al-tafsir): Clarification that explains an ambiguous or unclear word (mujmal or mushtarak) by specifying its intended meaning.
بيان تغيير (bayan al-taghyir): Clarification that changes the meaning of the original statement, such as through exception, condition, or limit.
بيان ضرورة (bayan al-darura): Clarification that arises due to necessity, e.g., when silence would cause misunderstanding.
بيان حال (bayan al-hal): Clarification derived from the speaker's state or circumstance.
بيان عطف (bayan al-'atf): Clarification by conjunction, where one part of speech clarifies another through connection.
بيان تبديل (bayan al-tabdil): Clarification by substitution, synonymous with abrogation (naskh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the logical division, which type of bayan is derived from the 'implication (lazim)' of the speech?
A) Bayan al-Taqrir
B) Bayan al-Tafsir
C) Bayan al-Taghyir
D) Bayan al-Tabdil (abrogation)

Key Takeaway
The logical division of bayan into seven types shows the systematic and inductive nature of Hanafi usul, where each type emerges from dichotomies based on the nature of the text.
